> ## Wisp
>*Small fey, neutral good*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 18
> - **Hit Points** 14 (4d6)
> - **Speed** 0 ft., fly 40 ft. (hover)
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|1 (-5)|26 (+8)|10 (+0)|13 (+2)|14 (+2)|11 (+0)|
>___
> - **Damage Resistances** acid, cold, fire, lightning, thunder; bludgeoning, piercing, and slashing from nonmagical attacks.
> - **Damage Immunities** poison, radiant
> - **Condition Immunities** exhaustion, grappled, paralyzed, poisoned, prone, restrained, unconscious
> - **Senses** darkvision 120 ft., passive Perception 12
> - **Languages** the languages it knew in life
> - **Challenge** 1/2 (100 XP)
> ___
> ***Ephemeral.*** The wisp can't wear or carry anything.
>
> ***Incorporeal Movement.*** The wisp can move through other creatures and objects as if they were difficult terrain. It takes 5 (1d10) force damage if it ends its turn inside an object.
>
> ***Variable Illumination.*** The wisp sheds bright light in a 5- to 20-foot radius and dim light for an additional number of feet equal to the chosen radius. The wisp can alter the radius as a bonus action.
>
> ### Actions
> ***Intertwine.*** The wisp enters the space of another creature and attempts entwine it in place. The target must pass a DC 12 Wisdom saving throw or be paralyzed for 1 minute. At the end of the target's turns, it can make another save, ending the paralysis on a successful one. While the wisp has a creature intertwined, attack rolls against it has disadvantage. If a target's saving throw is successful or the effect ends for it, the target is immune to this wisp's intertwine for the next 24 hours.
>
> ***Renew (Recharge 5-6).*** One plant that the wisp can see within 5 feet of it is renewed by the wisp; the wisp disappears. The wisp can't be targeted by any attack, spell, or other effect while renewing a plant. The renewed plant regains 10 hit points at the start of its turn. If the plant takes fire damage, the renew doesn't function at the start of its next turn. The plant dies if it starts its turn with 0 hit points.
> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The renew lasts until the renewed plant drops to 0 hit points, the wisp ends it as a bonus action. When the plant takes damage, the wisp must pass a Concen&shy;tration saving throw (as if concentrating on a spell) or be pushed out of the plant.

\columnbreak

<div style='margin-top:700px;'></div>

> ##### Will of the Forest
> Five wisps within 30 feet of each other are able to cast powerful spells. Each of the five must use its action and movement on three consecutive turns to call upon the powers of Elune and must maintain concentration while doing so (as if concentrating in a spell). When all five have finished their third turn of the ritual, the wisps gain the Spellcasting trait and can cast one spell in total at a target or point within 120 feet, no matter the spells normal range.
>
> ***Innate Spellcasting.*** The wisps spellcasting ability is Wisdom (spell save DC 12). They can innately cast one of the following spells as a 4th-level spell, requiring no material components. If a spell requires centration, all five wisps concentration must be broken to remove the spell:
> <div style='margin-top:0px;'></div>
>
> 1/ritual: *banishment, charm monster, confusion, <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; dispel magic, spike growth, wind wall*

> - **Damage Resistances** acid, cold, fire, lightning, thunder; bludgeoning, piercing, and slashing from non&shy;magical attacks and weapons that aren't silvered

> - **Condition Immunities** charmed, exhaustion, grappled, paralyzed, petrified, poisoned, prone, restrained
> - **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 12
> - **Languages** the languages it knew in life
> - **Challenge** 5 (1,800 XP)
> ___
> ***Incorporeal Movement.*** The wraith can move through other creatures and objects as if they were difficult terrain. It takes 5 (1d10) force damage if it ends its turn inside an object.
>
> ***Sunlight Sensitivity.*** While in sunlight, the wraith has disadvantage on attack rolls, as well as on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on sight.
>
> ### Actions
> ***Life Drain.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, reach 5 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 21 (4d8 + 3) necrotic damage. The target must succeed on a DC 14 Constitution saving throw or its hit point maximum is reduced by an amount equal to the damage taken. This reduction lasts until the target finishes a long rest. The target dies if this effect reduces its hit point maximum to 0.
>
> ***Create Spawn.*** The wraith targets a humanoid within 10 feet of it that died a violent death and has been dead for no longer than 1 minute. The target's spirit rises as a wraith spawn in an unoccupied space by the corpse, under the wraith's control. The wraith spawn has the same statistics as the wraith, except that it has an Intelligence and Charisma score of 1, it cannot speak or use Create Spawn, and its Life Drain does not reduce a target creature's hit point maximum. The wraith can have no more than two wraith spawns active under its control at one time.

## Gnolls
Gnolls are feral humanoids that attack settlements along the frontiers and borderlands of civilization without any warning, though highly aggressive, they are notorious for being extremely unintelligent and prone to infighting.

***Nomadic Destroyers.*** Gnolls are dangerous because they strike at random. They emerge from the wilderness, plunder and slaughter, then move elsewhere. They attack like a plague of locusts, pillaging settlements and leaving little behind but razed buildings, gnawed corpses, and befauled land. Gnolls choose easy targets for their raids. Armored warriors holed up in a fortified castle will <br> survive a rampaging gnoll horde unscathed, even as the towns, villages, and farms that surround the castle are ablaze, their people slaughtered and devoured.

Gnolls rarely build permanent structures or craft anything of lasting value. They don't make weapons or armor, but scavenge such items from the corpses of their fallen victims, stringing ears, teeth, scalps, and other trophies from their foes onto their patchwork armor.

***Intelligent Beasts.*** Gnolls are by no means an intelligent humanoid race, but rather many would call them relatively intelligent beasts. They are known to manipulate each other into fights over ridiculous things like *whose shadow is larger*. Gnolls use as much time to fight with each other as they do when fighting a common foe. The gnolls would be a fearsome race, if they ever stopped tearing each other to pieces long enough to organize into an army.

***Hunger for Meat.*** To a gnoll, meat is meat, and they will gnaw their victims bones clean of anything that resembles meat. Gnolls will even go so far as to kill and cannibalize outcasts of their pack if they are hungry enough. They've also made a tradition of devouring the bodies of their dead.


### Gnoll Brute
The strongest of the pack becomes those who lead it, a gnoll brute displays immense strength far superior to that of most gnolls. A gnoll brute is no more intelligent than any other gnoll, and only has a larger lust for blood.

### Gnoll Mystic
Some gnolls feel a connection towards the shamanistic forces of the world, these gnolls become mystics of their packs. A gnoll mystic is capable of performing simple arts of magic that would be considered novice by most scholars, but even though their feats aren't extraordinary they are held in high regard by gnolls of their pack, seeing them as being the wisest of beings.

### Gnoll Pack Lord
The alpha of a gnoll pack is the pack lord, ruling by might and cunning. A pack lord earns the best of a gnoll pack's spoils, food, valuable trinkets, and magic items. It places ornaments on its body of brutal piercings and grotesque trophies to show its superior strength over the pack.

## Golems
Golems are made from humble materials—flesh and bones, metal and stone—but they possess astonishing power and durability as their creation is wrought with magical energy. A golem has no ambitions, needs no sustenance, feels no pain, and knows no remorse. They are constructs created with a purpose in mind, to follow its creator as a guardian, protecting a person, place, or thing, or as constructs of war created to attack and defend at their creator's orders.

***Blind Obedience.*** These constructs are created to perform the task at hand flawlessly. If the golem is left without instructions, it continues to follow its last orders to the best of its abilities. When it is unable to fulfill its given orders, a golem might turn to violence, or stand and do nothing until new orders are given.

A golem can't think or act for itself. Though it understands its commands perfectly, it has no grasp of language beyond that understanding, and can't be reasoned with or tricked with words.

***Constructed Nature.*** A golem doesn't require air, food, drink, or sleep.

### Arcane Golem
Arcane golems are hulking, magically-empowered golems created to act as peacekeepers and defenders. Their large stone builds boast with magical energies inlaid through their bodies, displaying glows in many different colors.

Arcane golems are a favor construct amongst blood elves for their magical tenacity and are found primarily through Quel'thalas as they patrol the streets, roads, and cities of their kingdom with vigilance.

### Harvest Golem
Resembling a giant scarecrow equipped with razer-sharp metal claws and possessed with blazing orange eyes. That is the visage Harvest Golem. These large and terrifying 'scarecrows' wreck havoc and terror across the fallow fields of Westfall. Where these golems came from or who their creator are is but a mystery to the working folk of Westfall, but their purpose quickly became apparent. These golems are programmed with a simple purpose, to hunt down and eliminate the humans inhabiting Westfall. 

They have brought caution to the fields of Westfall and the many scarecrows that stand atop them, eliciting terror in anyone foolish enough to roam its fallow fields alone.

## Grell
A grell is a small, long-armed forest spirit with pointed ears and accentuated brows. Though their appearance carries an uncanny resemblence to imps, they are fairly large by comparison and lack any of the typical features of a demon.

Among explorers, researchers, and naturalists, it is speculated that the similarities between grells and imps are not coincidental, and that the first imps were in fact grells given into demonic influence during the first invasion of the Burning Legion. Such theories are widespread, but have never been confirmed nor denied.

***Wild Presence.*** Most grells have skin in shades of green, orange, or brown, mimicking the wilderness around their dwelling. Their arms and legs are covered in dense fur, and their hands and feet are all equipped with sharp claws. It is fairly common for grells to fashion themselves simple clothes, as well other adornments -- such as rings for their ears and nose.

Some have speculated as to whether these adornments serve a purpose, such as magical foci for casting spells, or if they are just for decoration.

***Fiendish Personality.*** It is said that the grell exist as an ebodiment of the wild, uncanny side of nature, and their personality shows this notion all too well. Grells on their own pose no particular danger to any would-be travelers, but a gang of grells working together can be a real threat to settlements and communities living close to their dwelling.

The most malicious grell are the ones who choose to roam around in packs, actively searching for straggling travellers to ambush, overwhelm, and steal from. Though their diet mainly consists of moss, tubers, and mushrooms, it is not unheard of for a pack of grells to hunt wild game.

## Harpies
Taking glee in suffering and death, the sadistic harpy is always on the hunt for prey. They are vicious predators that have lured countless adventures to their death, drawing them into the depth of their nest to kill and consume.

A harpy combines the body, legs, and wings of a hunting bird with the torso, arms, and head of a night elf. Its wicked talons and graceful wings make it a formidable threat in combat, and its eyes reflect the absolute evil of its soul.

***Noxious Nests.*** Harpies nest in hard-to-reach places from where they can terrorize the land around them. They slowly destroy the environment in which they settle, killing every creature they encounter and despoiling the land to build nests noted with their noxious order. Active nests are easy to discern by the intolerable smell and rot that protrudes from inhabited nests.

***Precious Collectors.*** These winged humanoids place great value on shiny baubles, valuable objects, rare gems, and ores. They are known to actively trade with nearby settlements to attain anything shiny, procuring a moments calm before they return to ravaging the land around them. The harpies adorn themselves with their shiny baubles and trinkets, as a show of their esteem.

***Beguiling Creatures.*** Harpies resembles malformed night elves combined with features of large predator birds. The sadistic creatures would be considered beautiful when seen from a distance and as they grow in age, they are known to become more beautiful. Growing to resemble formidable and colorful night elves more as they grow old.

Harpies are incapable of producing male children and their eggs will always hatch females. Because of this they have had to count on their cunning and deceptive nature to lure and capture males of many races for them to breed with. The males fill the role for a time, after which they become food for the nest.

### Harpy Witch
Some harpies are capable of wielding the forces of nature at their will. These harpy witches are powerful individuals within their nest, often using their aided forces of nature to rise to become queen of a nest and maintaining the title by tormenting countless enemies and allies alike to stay in their seat of power.

> ##### Variant: Beguiling Harpy
> Some harpies can have a special ability that allows them to charm humanoids.
>
> ***Innate Spellcasting (2/day).*** The harpy's can innately cast *charm person*, requiring no material or somatic components. Its spellcasting modifier is Wisdom.

## Kobolds

Diminutive, rat-like, and subterranean, kobolds can be found dwelling in sprawling caverns and abandoned mines across Kalimdor and the Eastern Kingdoms alike. Even throughout Northrend one can find their aptly named cousins; the snobolds. As far back as the first human settlements in the Eastern Kingdoms, kobolds have been a persistent, and annoying, presence.

Kobolds averages at four feet tall, with coarse skin, sharp claws, a pronounced snout, and a spindly tail. Educated guesses have pinned them as a distant offshoot from the troggs, though this has never been deemed certain.

***Skittish Creatures.*** Adventurers who have encountered a kobold, especially a kobold away from its pack and lair, can testify to their notorious cowardice. Kobolds are not particularly intelligent, and many consider them more of a nuisance than real danger -- at least in smaller numbers.

***Massive Flocks.*** Kobolds are not only known to bear a resemblance to vermin; they breed like vermin as well. Wherever one kobold can be found, hundreds more are likely not too far behind. While kobolds aren't considered a threat in smaller numbers, a pack numbering in dozens, even hundreds, can pose a threat even to seasoned adventurers if attempted removed from their dwellings.

They have no concept of marriage, rather, they form a loose structure of packs and clans based on lineages, with young individuals opting to migrate between nests and warrens in search of mates outside of their own family.

Famously, kobolds can become very protective of their belongings, and prefer to keep a distance from other races in order to keep themselves safe.

***Candle-Hoarders.*** Despite living deep underground, populating self-made caverns and abandoned mines -- sometimes even chasing miners away if the pack is large enough -- kobolds do not see well in the dark. They rely on candles to traverse whichever caverns they call home. 

These candles are usually made by the kobolds them&shy;selves, twining wicks from their hairs and pulling wax from their ears, though in desperation a kobold may contemplate stealing candles from other nearby settlements. Once a candle has been acquired, it is placed atop the kobold's head and left to burn there.

***Legends of the Darkness.*** Kobold legends speak of a dark, devouring presence dwelling in the deep places of the world, giving reason to the creatures' candle obsession.

To the same end, some kobold packs have been seen keeping rats as pets, as the critters do not fear the dark&shy;ness themselves. A well-trained rat can keep the kobold company and help out with digging, while a not so well-trained rat can make for a good dinner.

\columnbreak

### Kobold Names and Language
Kobolds typically speak Low Common, and often adopt other wide-spoken languages in the regions they dwell. The latter is especially prevalent across the Eastern Kingdoms, where most kobold packs and clans have learned Common over their long history of interacting with humans.

Kobold names and clan names are a descriptive amal&shy;gamation of everyday words. Kobold name usually has two parts; a short, easily vocalized first name, and a descriptive surname. Kobold surnames are personal and not inherited, but rather like a title that sums up their character, appear&shy;ance, or a well-known possession of theirs.

Their clan names often refer to common traits passed down through that clan's lineage, or to quirks unique to their society, though they can be hard to distinguish from the names the kobolds give themselves.

<div style='margin-top:-5px;'></div>

**Kobold Names:** Bukk, Feb, Feez, Gik, Kubb, Mlepp,
<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Naal, Slag, Znaz, Zniv
<br /> **Kobold Surnames:** Fatcandle, Flintdagger, Goldtooth,
<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Halfcandle, Luckybristles, Onetooth, Skullhat
<br /> **Clan Names:** Bluewax, Boulderslide, Gravelsnout,
<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Mudwhisker, Skywhisker, Windshear

>
> On a successful save, if another creature was responsible for the loss of candlelight, the kobold deals an extra 4 (1d6) damage when it hits that creature with a melee attack.

## Kodos
A kodo is a giant reptilian beast with thick <br> hide, immense strength and horns growing <br> out above its nose. These large beasts wander <br> the plains in thunderous herds, grazing as they <br> go along. Even though they have immense <br> strength, they are peaceful creatures who <br> doesn't use violence to solve conflicts between <br> themselves, but will defend themselves vigorously <br> if threatened by outsiders.

***Herd Animals.*** Kodos are pack animals and <br>move as a herd across grasslands and plains. A clear line of authority is apparent within the herd and it is formed as to protect the weak and young, and never to leave anyone behind. Most herds consists of a small dozen of kodos, but there has been sightings of herds so large as some fifty kodos. A herd leader is often an ancient kodo.

***Tauren Culture.*** The kodo beasts are key to tauren culture. Tauren hunt and use every part of kodos for their equipment, clothing, and food. But also train the mighty beasts as mounts or beasts of burden. The tauren see these creatures as a symbol of vigor and power, and hunting them is an important rite of passage for young warriors.

***Pack Beasts.*** Kodos are formidable pack beasts and are used extensively by the tauren, as well as other races of the horde. The large beasts are capable of carrying immense amounts of load for long period without being exhausted.

## Lashers
A lasher is a large slithering flora that can be found across Azeroth, although most lashers are not hostile, they will defend themselves fiercely if disturbed, using their long tendrils to lash out against their target.

***Sentient Plants.*** Lashers are the result of nature magic having seeped into the ground and corrupting the land around it, granting them the sentience to move on their own and pull themselves out of the earth. 

The magic of the earth affects the lashers tremendously. It has turned many lashers from their peaceful way into very hostile creatures corrupted by the magic around them.

***Adaptive Plants.*** These living plants can be found throughout Azeroth, lashers are capable of adapting to the environment around them to survive and sustain them. The plant their seeds wherever magic is apparent and protect them as the seeds grow into small lashers.

They plant their seeds  wherever possible and protect them as they grow to maturity.

***Fast Learners.*** These plants know near nothing but how to survive when they reach the maturity of their seed and become lashers. But these plants have shown an incredible ability of learning new skills like how to create small pieces of arts, set up and conceal traps, and gestures others might've shown them.

### Lasher Spitter
A lasher spitter is a large carnivorous plant capable of a vile acidic mixture within its stalk, these lashers are easily recognizable by the large maw that makes up the head of the plant. They are able to spit their toxic mixture onto nearby creatures and have it slowly dissolve their flesh.

### Barbed Orchid
A barbed orchid stands out from other lashers by its large flower head with the bead of an owlbeast placed in the flowers center. These lashers make dangerous combatants with their barbed edges striking back at attackers.

### Bloodpetal Flayer
At a glance most would take the bloodpetal flayer for a very colorful lasher, but nothing more. These lashers are much more ferocious and carry a vile toxin within their thorns that burns beneath a creatures flesh when injected.

> ##### Variant: Mature Lasher
> When lashers reach maturity, some learn to channel the powers of the moon in their favor. 
>
> A mature lashers has the same statistics as a lasher spitter, except that it has a Wisdom score of 12, and replaces the spitter's action options with the following action options
>
> ***Dream Lash.*** *Ranged Spell Attack:* +3 to hit, range 15/30 ft., one target. *Hit:* 5 (1d10) radiant damage.

>
> ***Miasma.*** When the gnome dies, toxic fumes spread in a 10-foot radius out from it. The fumes spread around corners and its area is lightly obscured. It lasts for 1 minute or until a strong wind disperses it. Creatures that start their turn in that area must succeed on a DC 11 Constitution saving throw or gain the radiation sickness. Read the Radiation Sickness sidebar for more information.
>
> ### Actions
> ***Shortsword.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +3 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 4 (1d6 + 1) piercing damage.
>
> ***Pistol (Recharge 5-6).*** *Ranged Weapon Attack:* +3 to hit, range 60/240 ft., one target. *Hit:* 6 (1d10 + 1) piercing damage.

\columnbreak

## Leper Gnome
Beneath the snow capped mountains of Dun Morogh lies the halls of Gnomeregan. It was once the capitol of the gnomes, but now its irradiated halls are home only to troggs and the crazed gnomes who survived the culling radiation of their once remarkable capitol.

Leper gnomes are gnomes contaminated by the toxic radiation of Gnomeregan. It has turned their skin a sickly green and dotted with abscesses that burst at the smallest strain they exert.

***A Necessary Sacrifice.*** When the gnomish capitol of Gnomeregan was invaded by hordes of troggs, the High Tinker ordered to cull the city and drive the troggs back by using the radiative waste previously contained within the machines of the city. Many more gnomes were killed than troggs when Gnomeregan was flooded by radiation.

Even worse, though, the gnomes who survived was horribly mutated and driven to madness by the radiation that sept into the city, changing them into what are now know as leper gnomes.

***Insane and Hostile.*** Fractious in groups and individually weak, most leper gnomes continue life in the poisonous halls of their city. Their minds are left crazed by the toxic fumes and have given them a tendency toward paranoia for the troggs which they now share the vast city with. They are hostile towards all intruder who dare enter their city, believing them to be trogg invaders or at best allied with the troggs themselves. Many of the leper gnomes know nothing else than the constant fear of troggs invading, and the few remaining survivors of the culling have lost their minds and memories of any other life.

***Mutated Creatures.*** The radiation has fundamentally altered the leper gnomes into something else and so far no cure to know to counteract the effect on them. The longer a leper gnome spend near radiation the more their body becomes a twisted and devolved. They continue to devolve further until they become mindless puddles of toxic sludge.

> ##### Radiation Disease
> When an uninfected creature comes into contact with a source of radiation, such as contaminated water—being bitten by an infected creature, or for every hour spent in an area of high radiation—the creature must succeed on a DC 11 a Constitution saving throw or contract the radiation disease.
>
> It takes 1d4 days for the disease to manifest. As it does the creature's skin gains a sickly green tint and abscesses start to spread across its surface. At the end of that period, the creature gains advantage on saving throws against poison and gains resistance against poison damage. The creature also has disadvantage on all Strength and Dexterity ability checks, and weapon attack rolls.
>
> Creatures who have carried the radiation disease for more than two weeks have their skin turn entirely green. The creature also no longer suffers from dis&shy;advantage on their ability checks or weapon attacks, and instead gain an indefinite madness. As described in the 5th Edition *Dungeon Master's Guide*.
>
> The radiation symptoms can be cured by spells such as *lesser restoration*. Once the disease has manifest, however, more powerful magic such as *greater restoration* or *heal* is required.

## Makrura
A makrura is a large aquatic race found living in small colonies along the coastlines of Azeroth and deep within the ocean. Makrura resemble enormous crayfish and observers have mistakenly called them *lobster men*.

***Aggressive and Hostile.*** A makrura within the confines of its colony is immediately hostile towards intruders and attempts to kill anyone that ventures to near. They use their massive claws to pinch their target, grappling them in place while the other tears the target into pieces.

***Wrecked Colonies.*** These large aquatic creatures create small colonies at the water’s edge or on the ocean floor. The makrura is unable to create sable homes are often settle in the wreckages of lost ships or underwater caverns.

***Savory Prey.*** The meat of a makrura has proven to be a  tasty treat to many races, and is appreciated all too well by creatures both on land and sea. Whilst some races on land hunt them for food, their most hated enemies are the ever present and notorious murlocs and nagas.

### Makrura Tidecaller
Some Makrura has an innate capacity for water magic and are able to call upon its forces, these makruras are called tidecallers. The makrura tidecallers call upon the waters to aid their allies and hamster their enemies if needed.

## Mana Wyrms
Manifesting near pockets of arcane energy, mana wyrms are small shimmering creatures that hover above the ground as they slither towards creatures or objects of arcane energy.

Rarely does the sight of a mana wyrm cause a seasoned adventurer concern, for them the small creatures are more of a nuisance than a threat and is easily avoided.

***Unstable Temperament.*** The temperament of a mana wyrm hangs solely on how long it’s been since it last fed on mana. These creatures are considered docile and harmless if fed often, but aggressive and unpredictable if hungry. The wyrms are also known for exploding in a flash of arcane.

***Arcane Sense.*** A mana wyrms can sense the taint and use of arcane energy near them and gravitate towards it, focusing their attacks against creatures that reek of arcane magic if hungry.

### Arcane Wyrm
An arcane wyrm is by many considered an overgrown mana wyrm that's been allowed to feed on too much energy before being put down. These long slithering creatures resemble large mana wyrms, and carry many of the same qualities as their kin. They are known for having a more even temperament than mana wyrms, and less prone to immediate hostility.

## Mechanicals
Mechanical constructs distinguish themselves from organic creatures mainly for their lack of blood, internal organs, and natural instincts. Instead, gears whirr and circuits spark inside these mobile machinations -- some of which act only at the behest of whoever holds the controls, while others have been configured to automatically carry out a pre-determined set of instructions.

Some mechanicals distinguish themselves further still, possessing instructions so meticulously crafted as to resemble genuine intelligence. As they are wholly driven by the logic of their configuration, mechanical constructs do not possess the ability to make an emotional response: they cannot be charmed, and they certainly cannot be frightened.

***Titanic Legacy.*** The origin of Azeroth's great mechanical achievements can be traced back to the titanic Watchers and the ordering of Azeroth. There, the titanic Keeper Mimiron oversaw the creation of a race of diminutive clockwork humanoids; mechagnomes, forerunners of the gnomes who now stand on the contested frontier of technological innovation.

***Gnomish and Goblin Ingenuity.*** Alongside the legacy of the gnomes, carrying on the work of the titanic Keeper who saw their creation, another source of technolgical innova&shy;tion on Azeroth has been the artifically enhanced ingenuity of the goblins. Unlike the gnomes, however, such goblin ingenuity has a tendency to be remarkably destructive. The two races have led a contested field of engineering, and have overseen countless mechanical wonders and mishaps across several decades -- including cities, transportation systems, explosive automatons, and giant death rays.

### Mechanical Animal Template
A mechanical animal is any Huge or smaller beast created by gnomes and engineers to resemble the shape of a beast found on Azeroth. The following characteristics change or are added to a mechanical animal when created.

***Retained Characteristics.*** The mechanical animal retains its Armor Class, hit points, Hit Dice, Speed, Strength, Dexterity, Constitution, vulnerabilities, resis&shy;tances, immunities, and special traits.

***Lost Characteristics.*** The mechanical animal loses its original saving throw and skill bonuses, and special sense. It loses any action that isn't Multiattack or a melee weapon attack that deals bludgeoning, piercing, or slashing damage. If it has an action or a melee weapon attack that deals some other type of damage, it loses the ability to deal damage of that type, unless the damage comes from a piece of equipment, such as a magic item.

***Type.*** The mechanical animal's type is construct, and it loses any tags it might have had.

***Alignment.*** The mechanical animal is unaligned.

***Ability Scores.*** The mechanical animal's ability scores change as follows: Int 3 (-4), Wis 11 (+0), Cha 1 (-5).

***Senses.*** The mechanical animal has 60 feet darkvision.

***Condition Immunities.*** The mechanical animal can't be charmed, frightened, paralyzed, petrified, poisoned, or gain exhaustion levels.

***Languages.*** The mechanical animal loses all languages it might've known, and understand the languages of its creator, but can't speak.

#### Sample Mechanical Animal
As an example, the Mechanostrider shown here uses the base statistics of a tallstrider.

### Alarm-o-Bot
These constructs are, as the name suggests, walking alarms. Originally by gnomes as a safeguard, to protect themselves against enemies hidding away in the dark, rugged terrain of their homelands, the alarm-o-bot keeps a constant watch for any sound or motion that it can discern with its numerous sensors. If it detects anything it cannot confirm as friendly, it blares out a high-pitched warning.

### Bombling
One of the original pinnacles of goblin engineering, bomb&shy;lings -- or bomb bots -- is a bomb affixed with a set of legs and a pair of eyes. Once a bombling has fixed itself onto a target, it gives chase until it gets close enough to detonate.

### Crowd Pummeler
A mechanical design adopted by both goblins and gnomes, crowd pummelers take the form of a tall bipedal construct loaded with heavy weaponry. Its name is not coincidental, as it is most commonly used as cheap, easily maintained sentries; programmable with a set of laws and regulations, and equipped with the chief directive to pummel anyone found to break said laws.

### Mechano-Tank
The Mechano-tank, or spider tank, is a gnomish construct best known for its armoured chassis and spider-like design. Built for close-quarters conflicts, most mechano-tanks come armed with fine-tuned and deadly weaponry. Their legs are able to contract and release, launching the tank forward into combat.

On a failed save, the creature can't use reactions, its speed is halved, and it can't make more than one attack on its turn. In addition, the creature can take either an action or a bonus action on its turn, not both. The effect lasts for 1 minute. The creature can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns.
>
> ***Nullify (Recharge after a Long Rest).*** The nullifier attempts to dispel all magical effects within 30 feet of it, as if it had cast the *dispel magic* as a 3rd-level spell on everything within range.
> <div style='margin-top:5px;'></div>
>
> The nullifier also gains the following reaction.
> <div style='margin-top:5px;'></div>
>
> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ***Reflection Field.*** When a creature hits the nullifier with a ranged spell attack, the nullifier can reflect the spell onto a target within 15 feet of it.

\columnbreak

<div style='margin-top:459px;'></div>

> ##### Crewing a Mechano-tank
> Most mechano-tanks are manual machines that require a pilot to operate, and even autopiloted tanks can be overwritten to work manually for a time.
>
> A creature can use its action to attempt to climb a **piloted** mechano-tank by succeeding on a DC 14 Strength (Athletics) check. On a failed save, the creature expends half its movement and is unable to climb the mechano-tank.
>
> The controls of the mechano-tank is sealed tight behind a hatch. The hatch can be opened with a successful DC 20 Strength check, or broken if dealt 20 bludgeoning, piercing, or slashing damage, it has an Armor Class (AC 15).
>
> A Small or smaller creature can expend 5 feet of movement to enter an unoccupied mechano-tank. A creature unfamiliar with the controls of tank must succeed on a DC 15 Intelligence check to under&shy;stand the controls of the machine before it is able to pilot it and control its actions and movement.
>
> While piloted, the mechano-tanks Intelligence, Wisdom, and Charisma scores are exchanged with those of the pilot. A piloted tank uses the initiative of its pilot. The pilot must use its action, reaction, and movement to use the machines action options or force it to move to a new location. While a crea&shy;ture is crewing the mechano-tank, it is considered to have full cover against any attack made against it from the ground.
>
> Taking control of an **autopiloted** tank requires a successful DC 17 Tinker's Tool Intelligence check. On a successful save, the creature takes control of the tank until the end of the creature's next turn. At which point the shredder’s failsafe mechanisms return, requiring a new save to temporarily take control of it.

A creature takes 18 (4d8) damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a success.

## Murloc
From a distance the degenerated fishlike humanoids that is murlocs might not seem like a big threat, but the small creatures are never alone and never far from their tribe and the water they inhabit. Their disgraceful and often humorous nature should not be underestimated cause behind their blank expressions lies a murderous mindset.

***Strange Territories.*** Murlocs populate coastlines, lake&shy;shores and swamps, never straying far from the land of their tribe. In more recent times, they have spread to many regions across Azeroth, inhabiting inland lakes and long secluded beaches.

Murlocs build strange chaotic villages of mud-and-twig huts that resemble structures more suited for the bed of the ocean than above the water. Their huts are scattered chaotically about without a discernible pattern, except for the prominent hut distinctly crafted for their oracle.

***Questionable Intelligence.*** Many races suggest that the murlocs are not particularly clever, considering their nearly impossible to decipher language. Others argue that, their ability to use weapons and their unusual fighting skills indicate a devilish smartness.

Murlocs are faithful creatures with a faith unlike any other. They worship entities of the sea, from the ordinary fish to huge elementals, and even prominent nagas. But their faith and belief in an entity is usually temporary and can change over the span of a week as events change.

***Pack Fighters.*** Even though murlocs aren't particularly brave, they will attack any traveler that approaches them if they can outnumber them.

Under pressure they flee to the water hoping for their foe to be foolish enough to follow them. Those who chase them underwater, regrets it as soon as they realize that there are several murlocs waiting in hiding, ready to attack quickly from all directions, like a swarm of hungry fish.

### Murloc Tidehunter
While many murlocs can use their intelligence to handle weapons to defend themselves, some of them are able to use their equipment to hunt. Being able to create nets and use them, tidehunters attacking in numbers, can be a serious threat to anyone foolish enough to pass through their territory. 

### Murloc Oracle
Even though most murlocs are raised to be warriors and hunters, few of them are born with a heightened willpower. Those murlocs, called oracles, are natural spellcasters. They are masters of the elements and can use them to control the environment around their enemies.

### Murloc Names and Language
Murlocs speak the Nerglish tongue, a strange language only spoken by aquatic creatures. Nerglish is a low aquatic language similar to Low Common and only spoken by a handful of lesser races.

Their names contain many wet, *soft* sounds; sh, i, and m are common amongst their names. Murlocs do not have individual surnames, instead they take the name of their tribe. Tribal names recall something of the tribe's accom&shy;plishments, appearance, history, or tradition.
<div style='margin-top:10px;'></div>

**Male Names:** Ashmol, Loshof, Molgoo, Shlesh
<br>
**Female Names:** Malash, Orgloom, Seeshen, Shyresh
<br>
**Tribe Names:** Blindlight, Bluegill, Greymist, Slatspittle

\columnbreak

## Nagas
The naga are former Highborne night elves who mutated into vengeful humanoid sea serpents. While many remain on Azeroth to attempt to reclaim the surface world, a large group followed Illidan Stormrage into Outland and proceeded to claim the watery areas of the shattered land.

***Mystical Culture.*** Naga culture is quite complex. Male naga are larger and more muscular, most of them serving as soldiers and guardians. 

Female naga are more delicate, with smaller scales and finer, more human-like faces. Naga women are natural spellcasters and rely on magic to defeat their enemies. Even though naga men are more numerous, the naga consider their women to be magically and intellectually superior. Their society is matriarchal, with women occupying most positions of leadership, and all naga paying homage to their queen, Azshara. 

***Altered Appearance.*** During the Great Sundering, Azshara and many of her Highborne followers fell into the depths of the Great Sea. Unable to avoid her death, Azshara forged a pact with an Old God, N'Zoth, trans&shy;forming her and her followers into the serpentine naga.

The naga are part night elf, part serpent, and some have evolved oceanic mutations. In all naga, many of these mutations are simply cosmetic — soft spines running down their backs, or extra fins adorning their arms. Some naga, though, also possess mutations that have a more substantial effect. 

***Azshara's Followers.*** All naga revere their queen, the mighty Azshara. They have never had another queen, and Azshara has become a living demigod for the naga. They do everything according to her design. 

Factions work continuously in bids for power, seeking the blessings of their queen. The vast majority of Azshara's servitors are willing to go to any means to elevate them&shy;selves in her eyes, even at the cost of their own lives.

### Naga Myrmidon
The myrmidons, with their navy blue skin and fearsome tridents, are among the strongest warriors in the naga's huge army. They are feared by all who dwell near the sea, most especially by the Makrura Empire.

Among their people, they are the most fanatically loyal to their beloved queen so much so that they no longer bother acknowledging orders, they simply do them.

### Naga Sea Witch
"Sea witch" is the informal term for a naga priestess of the tides. These scaly denizens of the ocean have often been associated with the coming of prodigious storms, but few have actually seen them rise from the sea and lived to tell the tale.

They are potent spellcasters, able to use terrifying frost and lightning spells against their foes. They also draw upon their race's arcane legacy to protect themselves.

<div class='letterheader'></div>
<div class="mmletter mml-n"></div>
<div class="pageLetter">N</div>
<div class='footnote'>NAGA </div>
<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/4C0c6NF.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:100px; right:-250px; width:800px' />

### Naga War Lord
Naga war lords are male naga warriors with stony arms  and shells fused to their skin. They have no visible eyes, and a large hermit crab for a hand. This may be resultant of their mutations, or they may be a different subspecies altogether.

### Naga Brute
Naga brutes are huge, mutated naga used as heavy fighters and even as siege weapons by the naga army. Some have rank, while some act more like mere beasts.

Each creature other than the naga in a 10-foot radius centered on the naga must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 31 (7d8) bludgeoning damage and is knocked prone. On a success save, a creature takes half as much damage and isn't knocked prone.

## Ogres
Ogres are large, brutish humanoids of immense strength native to the crumbling world of Draenor, many ogres have now settled as independent clans on Azeroth. The average adult specimen stands between 9 and 10 feet tall and weighs close to a thousand pounds.

Ogres believe the most important physical attribute is size and eschew garments that cover too much skin. Many instead adorn their skin with fearsome warpaints.

***Distant Settlements.*** After the Horde's second defeated attempt at invading Azeroth, the ogre clans of Draenor dispersed in all directions to establish dominance of their own in this new world. Few returned to Draenor, and many made the difficult journey across the great sea to Kalimdor. 

Ogres have settled throughout all of Azeroth and can be found in the furthest corners of the world.

***Clan Culture.*** Ogres have long since lived in large clans in which physical strength is greatly respected, and besting a rival is usually the only way to advance within the clan. 

Even though physical strength is seen as being the <br> most important attribute in their societies, the <br> powerful and keen minded ogre magi's often <br> enjoy an elevated position within a clan <br> due to their magical abilities.

***Brutish Combatants.*** The low intelligence <br> of most ogres push them towards simple and <br> straight forward solutions when they engage in <br> combat, often suffering as much punishment as <br> they dish out, relying on their strength and <br> stamina to keep them victorious at the battles end.

They are vicious opponents with the strength to rip off an opponent’s limbs should they so choose. Most favor heavy spiked clubs and mauls capable of bashing in the skull of their target and bring down heavy the heavy prey they hunt.

### Ogre Magi
An ogre magi is an ogre with an intelligence unlike that of most of its kin. Many ogre magi is the product of magic itself and came into existence during the Horde's second invasion of Azeroth, these hulking ogres sprouted a second head rumored to be the source of their keen mind and affinity for arcane magic. Although most ogre magi's have two heads, individual ogres have proven capable of making the incantations required to cast spells like those of a Magi.

### Ogre Lord
Ogre lords are hulking ogres that towers above the heads of regular ogres, these hulking monsters have no unique powers or special affinity towards arcana, but a strength and size without equal in the clan that has made them able to best rivals and always come out victorious. These ogres are able to wield clubs the size of tree-trunks and bash them against their enemies with an unmatched fury.

## Owlbeasts
An owlbeast is a serene and powerful creature <br>that inhabits forested regions of the world. They <br>resemble a cross between a bear and an owl, and <br>with the antlers of a great stag. Its strong claws and <br>hooked beak suggest a violent being, but its large golden eyes show its gentle nature.

***Forest Settlers.*** Owlbeasts live within the depths of forested regions, finding shelter in rocky terrain and uninhabited caverns. Owlbeasts are social creatures and live in small colonies within themselves. With no apparent structure of leadership, they live a harmonious lifestyle.

***Peaceful Creatures.*** Most owlbeasts treat peaceful travelers with as much respect as they are shown, occasio&shy;nally coming to their aid or assisting lost visitors by showing them safe roads out of their forests. Although owlbeasts are respectful of others who wander the forests, they show extreme ferocity against those who do not heed their gentle declines or openly show them hostility.

***Elune's Creation.*** Night elves and druids alike claim that the goddess Elune created the first owlbeasts in the early days of the world to serve as guardians to Cenarius. Combi&shy;ning the best traits of the owl, the most beloved of her night birds, and the bear, the lumbering protector of the woods. Resulting in the swift, elegant, and fiercely loyal hunters

But through the ages, the owlbeasts have grown more feral in their nature, and without the guidance of the goddess many are confused. They wander without purpose, though some find their way back to the sacred areas that they once swore to protect.

***Corruptible Minds.*** Owlbeasts are by nature peaceful and calm, but they are not the strongest mental creatures on Azeroth, and their minds have shown to be easily corrupted by greater powers, turning the calm owlbeasts into ferocious and easily aggravated beasts that can turn against visitors at a moment’s notice.

<div class="pageLetter">O</div>
<div class='footnote'>OWLBEASTS</div>

### Owlbeast
Owlbeasts are considered much more feral than the calm and peaceful moonkin, these creatures are more prone to be aggravated and go into an enraged stage where no sense can be made with them. They settle in large packs wherever they find shelter, even if it brings them into close contact with more sentient race, forcing them to fight for their home or find somewhere else.

### Moonkin
The mighty moonkin are claimed to be Elune's creation, these creatures appear similar to a simply owlbeast when first encountered, and could easily be mistaken for such. While owlbeasts trespass the border into feral beasts. A moonkin is a sentient creature capable of rational thinking and coherent conversation. Moonkin are blessed by Elune to spread nature's grace wherever they settle, and when threatened they exert the full force of the moon goddess.

## Quilboars
A ferocious, suicidally brave race with an alien mentality and devotion to their tribe, quilboars are stubby hunched humanoids with a pig-like face and rows of sharp spines running down its muscular back.

Quilboars have worn down brown skin adorned with tribal markings and tattoos, long razer-sharp quills runs the length of their back in place of hair. Multiple sets of stubby tusks protrude from the side of their mouth.

***Sacred Settlements.*** Quilboars live in the shade and protection of enormous roots that mar the land and choke out other life, turning the earth around them barren. The quilboar tribes flock to the thorny areas of central Kalimdor believe the regions to be sacred, and the erupted roots to have grown from the blood of Agamaggan.

When quilboars have turned a land too barren for them to settle in, their tribe moves on to find new areas to hunt in and their mighty thornweavers seed and grow new roots for them to live in.

***Hostile Colonies.*** These pig-like humanoids live in large colonies within their sacred thorn settlements. They are fiercely loyal to their colony, and defend it with reckless ferocity when nearby denizens venture too close to the thorns that mark their territories.

***Crude Shamanism.*** Quilboars practice a crude form of shamanism, weaving its forces together with druidic magic to make their mighty thornweavers. These shamans are kept in high regard by their colonies, and are seen as the voice of Agamaggan.

Quilboars revere the ancient Agamaggan as their creator and deity. Calling upon his aid to bolster them in fights and making sacrifices in his name. His blood would grow the twisted thorns of Razorfen, and his remain would adorn its entrance. All quilboars consider it to be a sacred place without equal on this earth.
### Quilboar Packmaster
Quilboars have a natural affinity towards boars, and some amongst them have made it their lives worth to raise and fight alongside such creatures. These packmasters are rarely alone, taking in the company of one or more boars wherever they go.

<div class='letterheader'></div>
<div class="mmletter mml-q"></div>
<div class="pageLetter">Q</div>

### Quilboar Thornweaver
The wise thornweavers are core to most quilboar colonies, these shamans are the voice of Agamaggan within a colony and their word is respected by all, and they are often close advisors of a colony's chieftain. In some colonies, the word of a thornweaver is placed above that of its chieftain and on rare occasions a thornweaver replaces a chieftain.

### Quilboar Chieftain
A quilboar chieftain rules over each colony, in most cases a quilboar became chieftain by overthrowing the colony's previous leader. They are surrounded by wise thornweavers and under rare circumstances a chieftain has one or more battleguards under their command. These brutish quil&shy;boars are the honor guards of a chieftain, and oversee the colony in the chieftains absence.

>

The creature can add a d4 to its rolls provided it can hear and understand the quilboar. A creature can benefit from only one Leadership die at a time. This effect ends if the quilboar is incapacitated.
>
> ### Reactions
> ***Quills.*** In response to being hit by a melee attack, the quilboar can spew quills back at the attacker. *Melee Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, range 10 ft., one target. *Hit:* 4 (1d4 + 2) piercing damage.

## Ravagers
Native to the world of Draenor, these quadrupedal beings roam the land surrounding them in search of food to fill their insatiable appetite, willing to dig their ragged teeth into any creature made of flesh.

Ravagers resemble giant insectiods equipped with ragged teeth and a carnivorous lust for meat. Their bodies are covered in hard chitin, combined with their surprising speed they make able fighters.

***Voracious Carnivores.*** Ravagers are able predators who hide behind rocks and in crevices until their quarry's within reach, only to emerge in great numbers and swarm around their prey to eliminate any possible escape. They ravage the land around them, extinguishing all potential life as they hunt for their colony's survival.

***Swarm Mentality.*** These large insectoids live in ever-growing colonies with the mentality of a large swarm.  They move as one, never leaving anyone behind and wander the land in search for food to survive. Although ravagers do not have an innate link like that of silithids, but they seem to be capable of predicting each others ideas and movements, mimicking them with immense precision.

***Migrated Creatures.*** Ravagers are native to the world of Draenor and have no equivalent on Azeroth. Yet they have found their way onto its surface through the crashed ship, Exodar. Stowaway beings on the ship, they had previously been captured and imprisoned, but the crashing of the ship allowed them to escape onto the shimmer isles west of kalimdors coast.

### Ravager Brood Mother
At the heart of a ravager colony sits the brood mother, she grants the colony life by laying the eggs that hatches into small ravager larva, blostering the colony's numbers. The brood mother is the queen of the colony and her survival means the survival of the colony as a whole, ravagers will go to extreme lengths to secure her safety.

### Ravager Wasp
Ravagers hatch as small insignificant larva that are quick to disappear into pupae, only to emerge as slender wasps with a swarm mentality and a ferocious sting. Wasps gorge themselves until their wings can no longer support their body weight, after which they undergo a third and final metamorphosis into the vicious four-legged ravagers.

> ##### Ravagers on alternate Draenor
> The ravagers of alternate Draenor were never exposed to the powers of fel, their bodies were not malformed. These creatures have evolved into large monsters more resembling four-legged spiders, their wings have grown with them giving all ravagers a flying speed equal to their normal speed.

## Sabercats
Sabercats are cunning felines that prowl across <br> Azeroth in their hunt for prey. These large proud, and magnificent felines have become a companion of many adventurers, and the demise of even more. <br> They are intelligent and loyal when domesticated, <br> but feral and quite aggressive when left in their <br> natural environments.

***Stalkers of Azeroth.*** Sabercats are found in many regions of Azeroth, but the vast majority of their kind can be found upon Kalimdor. The feline creatures have each adjusted to their various climate, sprouting pelts to help them blend in, and adapting to their surroundings. 

Many species of sabercats exist, each having adapted <br> to their climate differently and act differently towards outsiders, the most common sabercats are: Dreadsabers, Frostsabers, and Nightsabers, as well as the magically enhanced Manasaber of Suramar.

***Supreme Predators.*** Sabercats are deadly hunters and display the pinnacle prowess when allowed. They are able to prowl up upon unaware prey with ease, even displaying great athletic and acrobatic capabilities if needed.

***Fierce Companion.*** Night elves have bred and trained sabercats as mounts and companions for war through the ages, the trained sabercats are always exclusively night&shy;sabers but exceptions have been made. Once domesticated or fully trained from a cub, these beasts are loyal to a fault and make for a life-long companion.

### Manasaber
A manasaber is a magically infused sabercat, these beasts have been locked away with the decaying Highborne of Suramar for thousands of years, slowly mutation through generations into creatures infused with arcane energy. Manasabers take the appearance of slender sabercats with magical runes of power dimly glowing across their pelt.

Most manasabers are domesticated having been trapped in close proximity with night elves for thousands of years, but feral manasabers still exist.

<br>

> ##### Variant: Sabercat Armor
> An armored sabercat has an AC based on the type of barding worn (see the *Player's Handbook* for more information on barding). The sabercat's AC includes its Dexterity modifier, where applicable. Barding doesn't alter the sabercat's challenge rating.
>

## Satyrs
An ancient curse afflicted a Highborne sorcerer, destroying and remaking him as the very first satyr. These demonic beings were once night elves of the kaldorei empire, but little of that heritage is left in the demonic bodies of the satyrs and now these creatures carry a hatred towards all.

***Cursed Affliction.*** During the War of the Ancients, the Highborne sorcerer Xavius was tasked with opening the portal that connect the Twisting Nether and Azeroth, a task he failed in accomplishing and his disembodied spirit tortured as punishment by Sargaras. Yet the creator of the Burning Legion saw use in Xavius still and created him a new body, the first satyr in existence.

Xavius was sent back to Azeroth to spread his cursed existence to the Kaldorei Empire, twisting and reshaping night elves into the demonic satyr race. Like Xavius, all satyrs have the ability to pass on their curse and the curse have continued to spread through the ages, although the curse has weakened over time and become less effective.

***A Burning Hatred.*** Satyrs are creatures of hatred; they were created out of hate and carry on that quality from their creator. Satyrs have a burning hatred for all other living creatures and especially their night elven kin. They are immediately hostile towards outsiders and attempts to manipulate or corrupt them if possible.

***Tainted Magic.*** These demonic creatures corrupt the land they walk on and drain its magic as if they were wielding the powers of fel directly. They feed off its purity, leeching and corrupting. The magic they drain is stored in their hooves; the satyr that has drawn the most magic are distinguished by their swollen, uncloven hooves.

***Frightful Fighters.*** Satyrs are not known for being an organized enemy with a strategy for battle. They live in smaller sects found in more remote regions of Azeroth. When the sentry sounds danger, every satyr in the sect is quick to throw themselves into battle without worrying for their own lives. They act like a horde of demons without a commander whose orders to follow. 

### Satyr Trickster
Some satyrs show a certain penchant for painful traps and ambushing their target, these satyrs are called tricksters. They revere and mimic their Lord, Xavius' abilities of manipulation, and take a more subtle approach when the horn of battle is sound, sneaking up on their enemies and stabbing them in the back in an attempt to take out the strongest target of the assault.

### Satyr Hellcaller
A satyr hellcaller is a spellcaster skilled in fielding the chaotic fel of the Burning Legion. Rather than summoning demons of the Legion, these warlocks manipulate the entropic fire of fel itself. They are larger and more imposing than a common satyr because of magic they have drained from the land.


\columnbreak

> Cantrips (at will): *fel flame, green-flame blade, mage <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; hand, shadow bolt*
> <br> 1st-5th level (2 3rd-level slots): *arms of hadar, <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; bestow curse, hypnotic pattern, scorching ray, <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ray of enfeeblement*
>
> ***Shadowmeld.*** The satyr can attempt to hide even when it is only lightly obscured by foliage, heavy rain, falling snow, mist, or other natural phenomena.
>
> ### Actions
> ***Multiattack.*** The satyr makes two attacks: one with its claw and one with its scimitar.
>
> ***Claw.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 4 (1d4 + 2) slashing damage.
>
> ***Scimitar.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 5 (1d6 + 2) slashing damage.

## Scourge
Free of the demonic masters that created them, the precursor of the Burning Legions invasion into Azeroth have gained a will of their own. Under the rule of the dread Lich King the Scourge have built up their power on the arctic continent of Northrend, spreading their influence throughout the continent and beyond to the Eastern Kingdoms and Kalimdor.

Terrifying and destructive, the Scourge consists of <br> creatures resurrected into undeath by necromancers devoted to the Lich King, twisting their forms into undead abominations raised for their dark lord's service. From the icy realm of Northrend the Lich King rules uncontested, unleashing his undead minions on the world.

***The Lich King.*** In an attempt to escape a shattering Draenor, the old shaman Ner'zhul was apprehended by <br> the demon lord Kil'jaeden. He tore the shaman's body <br> apart, but kept his spirit intact and aware. Kil'jaeden <br> offered Ner'zhul his last chance to serve the Burning <br> Legion. The old orc agreed, his spirit was trapped within <br> a block of ice warped by the demon lord's chatoc powers.

Encased in a block of ice the Lich King was sent to Azeroth, landing in the frozen wastelands of North- <br> rend. Here, the spectral being of unfathomable power would begin the formation of the Undead Scourge. From his frozen throne of Northrend, the Lich King extended his will across the land to form his Undead Scourge, ever mindful of Kil'jaedens schemes as he in secret sought a way out of his icy prison.

In his search for a way out of his prison, the Lich Kings attention was eventually drawn to the prince of Lordaeron, Arthas Menethil. A capable warrior who had taken up arms against the seemingly endless assaults of his Scourge. Arthas grew increasingly restless as he pushed back against the Scourge, eventually tracking the origin of its plague to Northrend. Intend on ending its threat forever he took up the cursed runeblade Frostmourne. Thought the sword did grant him great power, the cost was high as Arthas began to lose his soul. Eventually completing <br> unholy transformation as his soul slipped away. He <br> became Ner'zhuls champion and would be a fearful <br> warrior leading the Scourge through its rampage at the <br> Lich Kings command. 

After countless battles, the demise of great and powerful individuals, leaders of kingdoms and commanders of the Burning Legion. Arthas would travel to Northrend and enter the hollow glacier that had become the Lich kings throne. With a cry of strength, Arthas would strike through the Lick Kings prison. As he placed Ner'zhuls thorny helm on his head, their spirits would fuse into a single mighty being, just as the Lich King had always planned. And thus one of the most powerful entities on Azeroth was born.

***Plague of Undeath.*** Ner'zhul needed to create an army, a vanguard for the Burning Legions invasion. For that he conjured the plague of undeath, a magical affliction that would spread across Lordaeron as a disease. Killing the afflicted and causing them to rise once more under Ner'zhuls influence. The plague was aimed at the human as of regions, but it afflicted much more than that, infecting flora and fauna and giving them strange symptoms of the plague itself, but rarely imminent death.

<div class="pageLetter">S</div>
<div class='footnote'>SCOURGE </div>
<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/rUSVZoq.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:0px; right:-300px; width:850px; transform:scalex(-1)' />
<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/5SuiuAg.png' style='position:absolute; top:0px; right:-50px; width:900px; transform:scalex(-1)' />
<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/JsVJeLH.png' style='position:absolute; top:0px; right:350px; width:px; transform:rotate(-5deg); filter:drop-shadow(1px 1px 4px rgba(0,0,0,0.42))' />

\pagebreakNum

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Since first conjured by Ner'zhul the plague has lingered in regions of Lordaeron, creating the plaguelands them&shy;selves. In the years following its use, others have attempted to use the plague of undeath as a weapon for their own benefit, some have tried to recreate its effects themselves.

***The Frozen Throne.*** The Icecrown Citadel dominates Northrend, visible from farther away than nearly any other structure and the home to the greatest army of undead in the known world. atop its glacial core sits dwells the Lich King, emitting his will across Azeroth to the commanders of the Scourge under his influence.

### Abomination
Twisted, mutilated creatures comprised of multiple dead limbs and body parts from different corpses. Abominations are not risen like so many other undead, they a created. Constructed out of putrid flesh, loosely stitched together to create enormous masses of rotting flesh. 

They are fearsome creatures that takes joy in carving the flesh from the bones of their quarry and lustfully eating it as if it was a delightful meal.

### Gargoyle
Unlike most creatures of the Undead Scourge, Gargoyles are not undead. These strange, wiry flyers are known for their rough, crystaline hides that protects them from all manner of attacks.

Stemming from the frozen northrend, gargoyles were brought to Lordaeron at Arthas' command as scouts in the army of the Scourge. Chaotic by nature, they have proven effective in their task and a frightful aerial combatant.

### Ghoul
Ravenous cannibals that leave only havoc and devoured corpses behind them. Ghouls are lumbering creatures of once innocent humans transformed into rotting corpses with a lust for flesh and terror.

They are a weapon of panic for the Scourge, a mindless vanguard made to terrorize settlements before the forces of the Scourge arrives. Made for the sole purpose of striking terror and doubt in settlements as they feast on the dead and living, friend and foe alike.

\columnbreak

### Scourge Risen Template
A creature risen by the scourge is any Huge or smaller creature brought back to life by vile necromantic energies. A creature that was never flesh and blood to begin with (such as a construct) can't be risen under the scourge's control. The following characteristics change or are added to a creature that becomes a scourge risen creature.

***Retained Characteristics.*** The risen retain its Armor Class, hit points, Hit Dice, Strength, Dexterity, Constitu&shy;tion, vulnerabilities, resistances, and immunities.

***Lost Characteristics.*** The risen loses its original saving throw and skill bonuses, special senses and special traits. It loses any action that isn't multiattack or a melee weapon that deals bludgeoning, piercing, or slashing damage. If it has an action or a melee weapon attack that deals some other type of damage, it loses the ability to deal damage of that type, unless the damage comes from a piece of equipment, such as a magic item.

***Type.*** The risen's type is undead, and it loses any tags.

***Alignment.*** The risen is neutral evil.

***Ability Scores.*** The risen's ability scores change as follows: Int 3 (-4), Wis 6 (-2), Cha 5 (-3).

***Senses.*** The risen has darkvision with a radius of 60 ft.

***Damage Immunities.*** The risen gains immunity to poison damage.

***Condition Immunities.*** poisoned.

***Languages.*** The risen understands all languages it knew in life, but cannot speak.

***Attacks.*** If the risen has no means of dealing damage, it can use its fists or limbs to make unarmed strikes. On a hit, an unarmed strike deals bludgeoning damage equal to 1d4 + the risen's Strength modifier, increasing by 1d4 for each size larger than Medium.

> ##### Variant: Greater Abomination
> A greater abomination has a challenge rating of 9 (5,000 XP). It has the statistics of an abomination except that it has 152 (16d10 + 62) hit points, Armor Class (AC 17), +10 to hit with its weapon attacks, and gains the following action options.
>
>***Engorge.*** The abomination makes one cleaver attack and places a grappled target in its ribcage. The target becomes restrained, and can use its action to break free by succeeding on a DC 17 Strength (Athletics) or Dexterity (Acrobatics) check. While restrained in this way, a creature takes 14 (4d6) bludgeoning damage at the start of each of the abominations turns. An abomination can have only one creature restrained within its ribcage.
>
> ***Cannibalize.*** The abomination cannibalize the corpse of creature that has been dead for less than 24 hours. Each creature of the abomination's choice that is within 120 feet and can see it must succeed on a DC 17 Wisdom saving throw or become frightened for 1 minute. A creature can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself on a success. If a creature's saving throw is successful or the effect ends for it, the creature is immune to the abomination's Cannibalize for the next 24 hours.

## Shale Spider
Shale spiders are durable diggers native to the elemental plane of Deepholm. It is the large stone spider’s tenacity and ferocity that makes other creatures fear them, even if they are harmed or pushed away, they will come back until someone has truly destroyed them.

***Stone Nuisance.*** The stone spiders often find their way out of the elemental plane of earth and into Azeroth, at first the spiders are more playful than anything, but their playful nature quickly changes as they get accustomed to their surroundings and gain their predatorial nature.

***Swarmers.*** Shale spiders are never alone, the earth is their family and the elemental spiders always has others nearby. They are notorious swarmers that work together to take down their prey.

***Elemental Nature.*** The shale spider doesn't require air, food, drink, or sleep.

> ##### Variant: Lava Spider
> A lava spider has adapted to burning climate around it, it drips molten magma as it skitters across the surface and illuminates its surroundings.
>
> A lava spider has immunity to fire damage, and gain the following additional trait:
>
> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ***Illumination.*** The spider sheds bright light in a 10-<br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; foot radius and dim light for an additional 10 feet.
>
> <br> The lava spider replaces the shale's action options has the following action options:
>
> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ***Multiattack.*** The spider makes one bite attack and <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; uses its Spit Fire.
>
> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; one target. *Hit:* 6 (1d8 + 2) piercing damage, plus <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 3 (1d6) fire damage.
>
> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ***Spit Fire.*** *Ranged Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, range <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 15/30 ft., one target. *Hit:* 9 (2d6 + 2) fire damage.

## Shredder
Large and impressive mechanical constructs, a shredder is a marvel of goblin ingenuity designed to replace lumber&shy;jacks and increase the profits of deforesting. These metal machines are often piloted by a creature crewed in its seat.

Shredders have made their way across Azeroth and can be found in the furthest of its corners where they work under the watchful eyes of goblin foremen as they harvest lumber, deforesting entire regions for their nefarious profit.

***Enemies of the Forest.*** Shredders are machines used to quickly and efficiently deforest entire regions, and because of this they have garnered a reputation and hatred amongst the creatures of the forest. 

Although the large shredders are mostly used for manual labor and harvesting, they often encounter resistance from creatures of the forest and are forced into fending them off. With their solid metal construction and great saw blades the machines have become great constructs of war, a fact their pilots makes good use of.

\columnbreak

<div style='margin-top:530px;'></div>

> ##### Crewing a Shredder
> Most shredders are manual machines that require a pilot to operate, and even autopiloted shredders can be overwritten to work manually for a time.
>
> A creature can use its action to attempt to climb a **piloted** shredder by succeeding on a DC 13 Strength (Athletics) check. On a failed save, the creature expends half its movement and is unable to climb the shredder.
>
> A Medium or smaller creature can expend 5 feet of movement to enter an unoccupied shredder. A creature unfamiliar with the controls of shredders must succeed on a DC 12 Intelligence check to understand the controls of the machine before it is able to pilot it and control its actions and movement.
>
> While piloted, the shredders Intelligence, Wisdom, and Charisma scores are exchanged with those of the pilot. A piloted shredder uses the initiative of its pilot. The pilot must use its action, reaction, and movement to use the machines action options or force it to move to a new location. While a creature is crewing the shredder, it is considered to have three-quarters cover against any attack made against it from the ground.
>
> Taking control of an **autopiloted** shredder requires a successful DC 14 Tinker's Tool Intelligence check. On a successful save, the creature takes control of the shredder until the end of the creature's next turn. At which point the shredder’s  failsafe mechanisms return, requiring a new save to temporarily take control of it.

## Silithids
Silithids are frightful insectoids living in large colonies beneath the crust of Azeroth. Although their individual strength is questionable at best, their collective hive mind is able to send warnings and pain surging through the hive.

Silithid can range drastically in size, beginning their life as small insignificant larva and growing into the swarms of insectoids that make up their race. Whatever their size may be, they all resemble massive insects. If those insects had mutated and desperately wanted to kill you.

***Spawns of Qiraji.*** As the kingdon of the aqir was left in ruins, those who remained would split in two and venture in opposite directions. One grouped traveled as far south as south goes and ransacked the research station near Uldum. Converting the titan facility into an extensive hive, renamed themselves the qiraji and their new home Ahn'Qiraj.

But their new hive held a dark secret, the facility had served as the prison of C'Thun, one of the Old Gods who had once reigned over primordial Azeroth. The arrival of the qiraji turned the facility from a prison into a seat of power. Worshiping the Old God as the aqirs had before them, the qiraji would become his servants and spent thousands of years building an army capable of exacting revenge upon the whole of Kalimdor.

To form this army C'Thun would create the silithid, a race of insectiod creatures born from the qiraji themselves. The silithid would grow and become an enormous force for Ahn'Qiraj to utilize as they  created their great empire.

***Bestial Drones.*** Unlike the qiraji, the silithid are not intelligent, sentient beings. C'Thun created them from the powers of the qiraji to become a mighty force for Ahn'Qiraj. Mindless bestial insectoids, minions that are eternally loyal to the qiraji and in turn C'Thun himself.

\columnbreak

<div style='margin-top:733px;'></div>

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; ***Collective Hive Mind.*** Although silithids might seem to be acting of their own accord, they are not sentient beings and work as a collective entity in their hive. This does not though make them any less dangerous. A hive of silithids is often controlled by one or more colossi exerting their will over the collective hive and directing their way of life.

The hive colossi's are in turn controlled by the powerful qiraji who exert complete dominance over the race shaped from their own beings. It is not uncommon for large hives to have a large crystalline prism deep within its core for the qiraji to communicate various messages through.

***Adaptable Hive.*** No other creature can adapt to changes in their environment as quickly as the silithid. Although adventurers foolish enough to delve into the hive of silithids in hopes of removing their colossi might think that killing the center of the hive mind will hamper the silithids. The larva can evolve into a variety of silithid creatures based on the needs of the hive and replenish any loss.

> ##### Variant: Hive Controller
> The strongest of a hive's colossi exerts direct command over other silithids in the hive. Usually this is either the hive lord, closest of the queen's consorts, or the hive queen herself. 
>
> The Hive Controller can be distinguished by its see-through cranium, leaving its brain visible. It has the following additional trait.
>
> <br>***Leadership (Recharges after a Short or Long Rest).*** For 1 minute, the silithid can send a telepathic command whenever a nonhostile creature that it can see within 60 feet of it makes an attack roll or a saving throw. The creature can add a d4 to its roll provided it can receive the command. A creature can benefit from only one Leadership die at a time. This effect ends if the silithid is incapacitated.

While swallowed, the creature is blinded and restrained, it has total cover against attacks and other effects outside the silithid, and it takes 21 (6d6) acid damage at the start of each of the silithid's turns.
> <br>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; If the silithid takes 30 damage or more on a single turn from a creature inside it, the silithid must succeed on a DC 15 Constitution saving throw at the end of that turn or regurgitate all swallowed creatures, which fall prone in a space within 10 feet of the silithid. If the silithid dies, a swallowed creature is no longer restrained by it and can escape from the corpse using 15 feet of movement, exiting prone.

## Skeletons
Skeletons arise when animated by dark magic. They heed the summons of necromancers who call them from their stony tombs and ancient battlefields, or rise of their own accord in places saturated with death and loss, awakened by stirrings of necromancy or presence of corrupting evil.

***Animated Dead.*** Whatever sinister force awakens a skeleton infuses its bones with a dark vitality, adhering joint to joint and reassembling limbs. This energy motivates <br>a skeleton to move and think in a rudimentary fashion, though only as a pale imitation of the way it behaved in life. Resurrecting a skeleton restores its body and soul, banishing the hateful undead spirit that empowers it.

While most skeletons are the animated remains of dead humans and other humanoids, skeletal undead can be created from the bones of other creatures besides human&shy;oids, giving rise to a host of terrifying and unique forms.

***Obedient Servants.*** Skeletons raised by spell are bound to the will of their creator. They follow orders to the letter, never questioning the task their masters give them, regard&shy;less of the consequences. Because of their literal interpre&shy;tation of commands and unwavering obedience, skeletons adapt poorly to changing circumstances.

A skeleton can fight with weapons and wear armor, can load and fire a catapult or trebuchet. Some are even raised with knowledge of their past life and become formidable warriors or mages able to perform complex incantations.


Although most lack the intellect they possessed in life, skeletons aren't mindless. Rather than break its limbs attempting to batter its way through an iron door, a skele&shy;ton tries the handle first. If that doesn't work, it searches for another way through or around the obstacle.

***Undead Nature.*** A skeleton doesn't require air, food, drink, or sleep.

<div style='margin-top:-15px;'></div>
